{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_018fccbVSaQHfZHnF7nqmiU3","type":"tool_result","content":"# Genetic variants in the KIF6 region and coronary event reduction from statin therapy\n\n## Metadata\n**Authors:** Yonghong Li, Marc S Sabatine, Carmen H Tong, Ian Ford, Todd G Kirchgessner, Christopher J Packard, Michele Robertson, Charles M Rowland, Lance A Bare, James Shepherd, James J Devlin, Olga A Iakoubova\n**Journal:** Human Genetics\n**Date:** 2010 Oct 1\n**DOI:** [10.1007/s00439-010-0892-6](https://doi.org/10.1007/s00439-010-0892-6)\n**PMID:** 20886236\n**PMCID:** PMC3016221\n**URL:** https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3016221/\n**PDF:** [https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC3016221/pdf/439_2010_Article_892.pdf](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC3016221/pdf/439_2010_Article_892.pdf)\n\n## Abstract\n\n**Electronic supplementary material:** \nThe online version of this article (doi:10.1007/s00439-010-0892-6) contains supplementary material, which is available to authorized users.\n\n### Electronic supplementary material\n\nThe online version of this article (doi:10.1007/s00439-010-0892-6) contains supplementary material, which is available to authorized users.\n\n## Introduction\n\nThe risk for coronary heart disease (CHD) varies between individuals and can be ameliorated by lifestyle changes and medications such as statins. Although statins have been shown to be highly effective in reducing CHD events in randomized controlled trials, individual response to statin therapy varies (reviewed in Mangravite et al. [2006](#CR12); Schmitz and Langmann [2006](#CR16)), a variability thought to be partly due to genetic factors.\n\nRecently, a common single nucleotide polymorphism (SNP) in *KIF6*, a member of the *KIF9* family of kinesins, has been reported to be associated with CHD risk and differential reduction of coronary events from statin therapy (Bare et al. [2007](#CR2); Iakoubova et al. [2008a](#CR6), [b](#CR7), [2009](#CR8); Shiffman et al. [2008a](#CR18), [b](#CR19)); this SNP (rs20455) encodes the missense polymorphism KIF6 Trp719Arg. In a meta-analysis of seven prospective studies, carriers of the 719Arg variant had over 20% increased risk of CHD, compared with non-carriers (*P* = 1.02 × 10^−6^) (Li et al. [2010](#CR11)). This increased risk was independent of traditional risk factors including age, blood pressure, diabetes, smoking, low-density lipoprotein cholesterol (LDL-C) or high-density lipoprotein cholesterol (HDL-C). However, an association between the *KIF6* Trp719Arg polymorphism and CHD was not observed in two case–control studies (Stewart et al. [2009](#CR21); Wellcome Trust Case Control Consortium [2007](#CR22)), possibly due to statin use.\n\nThe 719Arg variant was also associated with greater reduction of coronary events from both pravastatin (a hydrophilic statin) and atorvastatin (a lipophilic statin) therapy. In retrospective genetic analyses of four prospective clinical trials, the Cholesterol and Recurrent Events trial (CARE) (Sacks et al. [1996](#CR14)), the West of Scotland Coronary Prevention Study (WOSCOPS) (Shepherd et al. [1995](#CR17)), Pravastatin or Atorvastatin Evaluation and Infection Therapy-Thrombolysis In Myocardial Infarction 22 (PROVE IT-TIMI22) (Cannon et al. [2004](#CR3)), and the PROspective Study of Pravastatin in the Elderly at Risk (PROSPER), carriers of the 719Arg variant (~60% of people of European ancestry) had substantial and significant reduction of CHD events from statin therapy, whereas non-carriers did not (Iakoubova et al. [2008a](#CR6), [b](#CR7), [2009](#CR8)).\n\nHere we have conducted a fine mapping study to determine (1) whether other SNPs or haplotypes in the *KIF6* region account for the association of rs20455 (Trp719Arg) with differential coronary event reduction from statin therapy and (2) whether other variants in the *KIF6* region are independently associated with differential reduction of events from statin therapy.\n\n## Methods\n\n### Study population\n\nThe populations in this genetic study were derived from three prospective double blind, randomized clinical trials that evaluated the effect of statin therapy on coronary events: CARE, PROVE IT-TIMI22, and WOSCOPS. CARE evaluated the effect of 40 mg/day pravastatin, compared with placebo, on the reduction of fatal CHD and nonfatal myocardial infarction (MI) in men and women with a prior MI and LDL-C levels between 115 and 174 mg/dL (average age of 59 years old); WOSCOPS evaluated the effect of 40 mg/day pravastatin, compared with placebo, on the reduction of fatal and nonfatal CHD in men with LDL-C levels between 174 and 232 mg/dL (age ranged from 45 to 64 years old) and no history of MI; PROVE IT-TIMI 22 evaluated the effect of intensive statin therapy (80 mg/day atorvastatin), compared with moderate statin therapy (40 mg/day pravastatin), on fatal and nonfatal cardiovascular events in men and women after acute coronary syndromes (average age of 58 years old). The average follow-up period was 5, 2 and 4.9 years for the CARE, PROVE IT-TIMI 22 and WOSCOPS trials, respectively. The current genetic analyses were performed in those patients whose DNA was available: 2,913 in CARE, 1,817 in PROVE IT-TIMI22, and 1,570 in WOSCOPS; note that for WOSCOPS we obtained access to a previously described nested case–control study that included all cases, who had CHD events and age- and smoking status-matched controls who did not have events during the WOSCOPS trial (Packard et al. [2000](#CR13)). This study was limited to Caucasian patients to avoid complications arising from potential differences in linkage disequilibrium (LD) structure in different populations and because each trial enrolled only about 10% or fewer non-Caucasian patients. Characteristics of the patients included in this genetic study can be found in Supplementary Table 1.\n\nThe endpoints were either the primary endpoint of the original clinical trials (for CARE and PROVE IT-TIMI22) or that of the previously reported nested case–control study of WOSCOPS (Packard et al. [2000](#CR13)). For CARE, the endpoint was fatal coronary event or nonfatal MI (Shiffman et al. [2010](#CR20)); for PROVE IT-TIMI22, the endpoint was death from any cause or major cardiovascular events including MI, revascularization, unstable angina requiring hospitalization and stroke (Cannon et al. [2004](#CR3)); and for WOSCOPS, the endpoint was CHD death, nonfatal MI, and revascularization (Shepherd et al. [1995](#CR17)). Genotypes were determined in a core facility by either allele-specific real-time PCR (Germer et al. [2000](#CR5)) or multiplexed PCR of genomic DNA followed by multiplexed allele detection (Iannone et al. [2000](#CR9)). Genotyping was carried out in plates with randomly arrayed samples, and genotype calls were made without the knowledge of the sample event status.\n\n### SNP selection\n\nThe interrogated region on chromosome 6 spanned from 39,392,028 to 39,809,728 bp, corresponding to the positions of rs1535500 and rs215497. This region includes the entire *KIF6* gene plus 8.6 kbp upstream and 18.8 kbp downstream of the *KIF6* gene (Fig. [1](#Fig1)). A total of 178 SNPs in this *KIF6* region were genotyped in CARE, including rs20455 and 26 other SNPs whose association with risk of CHD had been investigated previously (Iakoubova et al. [2008b](#CR7)). Of the 178 SNPs included in this study, the genotype distributions of five SNPs did not meet Hardy–Weinberg expectations (*P* < 0.001) and three SNPs had an allele frequency less than 2%; the remaining 170 SNPs were analyzed for association with differential coronary event reduction from statin therapy. All 450 SNPs in the *KIF6* region in the HapMap dataset (de Bakker et al. [2005](#CR4)) with an allele frequency greater than 2% were either included in these 170 SNPs or in LD (*r* ^2^ > 0.8) with one of the 170 SNPs.\n\n### Fig. 1.\n\n![Fig. 1](https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/8c81/3016221/07b0514d8c8c/439_2010_892_Fig1_HTML.jpg)\n\nLinkage disequilibrium and association with statin therapy in CARE. Gene and SNP locations and SNP to SNP LD in the HapMap dataset (in D′ ranging from 1 in red to 0 in white) in the KIF6 region are shown in the lower part of the figure. The LD block containing rs20455 is indicated with a green bar. LD between rs20455 and other genotyped SNPs in CARE is shown in the middle part of the figure. Nucleotide position on the chromosome is indicated below the x axis in kilobases. Association between SNP and event reduction in CARE (dominant model P interaction) is presented in the top panel\n\nOne objective of the current study was to determine the presence of a SNP in the *KIF6* region that could explain the association of *KIF6* Trp719Arg SNP with differential reduction of coronary events from statin. Therefore, to avoid missing such a hypothetical ‘causative’ SNP that, by chance, had a weak association in one of the studies we set a relaxed threshold (*P* _interaction_ < 0.1) for advancing SNPs from one study to the next. Therefore, the flow of the study was as following: SNPs were first tested in CARE, and those that were associated with differential reduction of events from statin therapy (*P* _interaction_ < 0.1) were then analyzed in PROVE IT-TIMI22. SNPs that were associated with statin response in PROVE IT-TIMI22 (*P* _interaction_ < 0.1 and hazard ratio in the same direction as in CARE) were further analyzed in WOSCOPS. We adopted this sequence of analysis partly because only a limited amount of DNA was available from patients in the WOSCOPS study.\n\n### Statistical analyses\n\nGenotype distribution in the individual studies was tested for deviation from Hardy–Weinberg equilibrium (HWE) by an exact test.\n\nFor each SNP, likelihood ratio tests comparing Cox (CARE and PROVE IT-TIMI22) or logistic regression models (WOSCOPS) with and without an interaction term between genotype and statin therapy were used to evaluate heterogeneity (measured by *P* _interaction_) of event reduction from statin therapy. Additive, dominant, and recessive models for each SNP were coded using the major allele (defined in CARE) as the reference allele so that the direction of estimated parameters would be consistently measured across all three studies.\n\nThe LD measure *r* ^2^ was calculated from unphased data with the LDMAX program in the GOLD package (Abecasis and Cookson [2000](#CR1)). Haplotype frequencies were estimated from the genotype data and, using the posterior probabilities of possible haplotype pairs for each subject, tested for association with heterogeneity of event reduction from statin therapy using logistic regression as implemented in the R package haplo.stats (Lake et al. [2003](#CR10); Schaid et al. [2002](#CR15)). A sliding window was used to select haplotypes consisting of three or five adjacent SNPs.\n\n## Results","is_error":false}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01XvieTbNbio1puo6Q4yDgjF","session_id":"d4943565-ecaf-4722-ae19-ced6837c5ba8","uuid":"84f103ce-3c1a-42b5-9808-6d271818ad68"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_014BUfvu9xBMhQbRwd7GL2eb","type":"tool_result","content":"To fine map the *KIF6* region, we analyzed 170 SNPs to determine whether reduction of fatal CHD or confirmed nonfatal MI events from statin therapy in CARE differed between genotype-defined subgroups as assessed by the interaction between genotype and treatment group (*P* _interaction_, see “[Methods](#Sec2)”). We found that 44 SNPs met the *P* _interaction_ threshold of <0.1 (Supplementary Tables 2, 3 and 4). Of the 17 SNPs associated with differential reduction of events from statin therapy in the recessive model, 16 SNPs were excluded from further analysis, because for each of these SNPs, fewer than 4% of the patients were minor homozygotes and there were very few events (<10) among the minor homozygotes. The remaining 28 SNPs (including rs20455) associated with differential reduction of events from statin therapy included 12 SNPs that were in LD with rs20455 and clustered in a 53 kbp region (Fig. [1](#Fig1), indicated by a green bar above the LD map).\n\nWe then analyzed these 28 SNPs in the PROVE IT-TIMI22 cohort using the genetic model for each SNP that was most significant in the CARE analysis. Six SNPs were associated with differential event reduction from statin therapy (*P* _interaction_ < 0.1) in PROVE IT-TIMI22, and event reduction from statin therapy was greatest in the same genotype for all six SNPs: 2 in the additive model and 4 in the dominant model (Supplementary Tables 5 and 6). Further analyses of these six SNPs in the WOSCOPS study showed that three SNPs (rs20455, rs9462535 and rs9471077) were differentially associated with coronary event reduction by statin use (*P* _interaction_ < 0.1, dominant model; Table [1](#Tab1); Fig. [2](#Fig2)). These three SNPs were in high LD with each other (*r* ^2^ = 0.84–0.98) (Supplementary Table 7).\n\n### Table 1.\n\n| SNP type | Study | Genotype | Drug* |  | Comparator* |  | Model 1** |  |  | Model KIF6 region with differential reduction of coronary events from statin therapy in CARE, PROVE IT-TIMI 22 and WOSCOPS studies\n\n### Fig. 2.\n\n![Fig. 2](https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/8c81/3016221/06d1fb95d7b7/439_2010_892_Fig2_HTML.jpg)\n\nEffect of statin therapy on coronary events stratified by the genotype of three SNPs in CARE, PROVE IT-TIMI22 and WOSCOPS studies. The hazard ratios or odds ratios were calculated for Model 2 in Table 1\n\nWe next carried out haplotype analyses in CARE in the 53 kbp region of high LD surrounding rs20455 (green bar in Fig. [1](#Fig1)) using a sliding window approach (Schaid et al. [2002](#CR15)). Results of haplotypes comprising three SNPs along with the results of the most significant individual SNP in a given haplotype are shown in Supplemental Fig. 1. In CARE, only the haplotypes based on rs45460596, rs9394585 and rs9357303 were more significantly associated with event reduction than the best of the three SNPs alone (dominant *P* _interaction_ = 0.0088 vs. 0.097); however, in PROVE IT-TIMI22 these haplotypes were not associated with event reduction (dominant haplotype *P* _interaction_ = 0.55). Testing of haplotypes consisting of five adjacent SNPs did not reveal any haplotype that was more significant than the corresponding individual SNPs (data not shown).\n\nWe also carried out a haplotype analysis in CARE of the three SNPs (rs9471077, rs9462535, and rs20455) that were associated with event reduction in all three studies. Two common (>5%) haplotypes were observed, which corresponded to *KIF6* 710Arg carriers and non-carriers (data not shown). Due to the high LD between these three SNPs, we were unable to differentiate the effects of one SNP from another despite exploring both pairwise adjustment and stepwise regression analyses. For example, there were only six events each in placebo and statin-treated subjects among the combinations where the genotypes are discordant (data not shown).\n\nSince rs20455 had also been reported to be associated with CHD, we analyzed association of the two other SNPs (rs9462535 and rs9471077) that were consistently associated with event reduction in CARE and WOSCOPS. We found that they were also associated with CHD (Table [2](#Tab2)).\n\n### Table 2.\n\n| SNP | Genotype | Study | Model 1* |  | Model 2** |  |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| HR or OR (95% CI) | P | HR or OR (95% CI) | P |  |  |  |\n| rs20455 | CT + CC versus TT | CARE | 1.54 (1.10–2.14) | 0.0112 | 1.48 (1.06–2.06) | 0.0215 |\n| WOSCOPS | 1.61 (1.19–2.17) | 0.0017 | 1.55 (1.15–2.10) | 0.0045 |  |  |\n| rs9462535 | AC + AA versus CC | CARE | 1.38 (1.00–1.92) | 0.0530 | 1.32 (0.95–1.84) | 0.0944 |\n| WOSCOPS | 1.57 (1.16–2.12) | 0.0036 | 1.53 (1.12–2.08) | 0.0069 |  |  |\n| rs9471077 | CT + CC versus TT | CARE | 1.44 (1.02–2.03) | 0.0376 | 1.38 (0.98–1.95) | 0.0678 |\n| WOSCOPS | 1.51 (1.12–2.05) | 0.0077 | 1.46 (1.07–1.99) | 0.0160 |  |  |\n\nTable 2 Caption: Association of the three SNPs in the KIF6 region and coronary events in the placebo groups of CARE and WOSCOPS\n\n## Discussion\n\nThis study was designed to investigate whether (1) the previously reported association of rs20455 (Trp719Arg) with coronary event reduction from statin therapy could be better explained by another SNP in the *KIF6* region and (2) other SNPs in the *KIF6* region were associated with coronary event reduction from statin therapy independently of rs20455. We found that two additional SNPs in strong LD with rs20455 were consistently associated (*P* _interaction_ < 0.1) with differential reduction of clinical events from statin therapy in the CARE, WOSCOPS, and PROVE IT-TIMI22 studies. These two SNPs are located in introns, while rs20455 is a missense polymorphism in the *KIF6* gene.\n\nPreviously, we have tested 27 SNPs, including rs20455, in a 95.5 kbp portion of the *KIF6* region (from position 39,347,330 to position 39,442,863 on chromosome 6) for association with CHD in the placebo arms of the CARE and WOSCOPS studies (Iakoubova et al. [2008b](#CR7)). This study expands the interrogated region and focuses on differential event reduction from statin therapy, an effect of particular clinical interest. The three SNPs that we found to be associated with differential response to statin therapy are highly correlated and thus indistinguishable from each other in this association. However, the possibility that the 719Trp versus 719Arg variation has functional consequences is supported by the BLOSUM62 score of −3 for this variation. The BLOSUM62 score is the log odds for amino acid substitutions in conserved protein blocks (Henikoff and Henikoff [1992](#CR100)), and a score of −3 indicates a less likely substitution. As the Trp719Arg substitution is near the putative cargo-binding tail domain of the kinesin, it would be interesting to determine whether the amino acid change affects the binding of cargo molecules by the KIF6 protein.\n\nOne limitation of our study is that we were unable to define the causal variant with certainty. Strategies to identify causal variants include performing genetic association studies in a different population that might have a distinct LD structure for these tightly linked SNPs from the initial studies. The CARE and PROVE IT-TIMI22 cohorts had small numbers of non-Caucasian participants; therefore, the power to conduct an association study in the non-Caucasian population is limited. Another limitation is that PROVE IT-TIMI22 may not be comparable to CARE and WOSCOPS—the former tested intensive statin therapy compared with moderate statin therapy, while the latter tested 40 mg/day pravastatin compared with placebo. Therefore, by including PROVE IT-TIMI22, we may have missed the SNPs that are capable of predicting event reduction response to pravastatin compared with placebo but not intensive statin therapy compared with moderate statin therapy. Such SNPs may be independent from rs20455, which predicts differential event reduction from both 40 mg/day pravastatin compared with placebo and intensive statin therapy compared with moderate statin therapy. In addition, PROVE IT-TIMI22 primary endpoint included a small fraction (5.2% of primary events) of death from presumably non-cardiovascular events, while the CARE endpoint and the WOSCOPS case definition did not include non-cardiovascular death.\n\nIn conclusion, we have identified three highly linked SNPs in the *KIF6* region that predict differential reduction of coronary events from statin therapy. Functional characterization of these variants is warranted and could help to explain the role of *KIF6* in the pathogenesis of CHD and the variable event reduction in response to statin therapy.\n\n## Electronic supplementary material\n\nBelow is the link to the electronic supplementary material.\n\n## Acknowledgments\n\nWe would like to express our gratitude to patients and clinical investigators of the CARE, WOSCOPS and PROVE IT-TIMI22 trials.\n\n### Open Access\n\nThis article is distributed under the terms of the Creative Commons Attribution Noncommercial License which permits any noncommercial use, distribution, and reproduction in any medium, provided the original author(s) and source are credited.\n\n## Associated Data\n\n*This section collects any data citations, data availability statements, or supplementary materials included in this article.*\n\n### Supplementary Materials\n\n### Supplementary Materials\n\n## References\n\n1. cancer patients\n\n**Authors:** Suman Lal, Zee Wan Wong, Edwin Sandanaraj, Xiaoqiang Xiang, Peter Cher Siang Ang, Edmund J D Lee, Balram Chowbay\n**Journal:** Cancer Science\n**Date:** 2008 Mar 28\n**DOI:** 10.1111/j.1349-7006.2008.00744.x\n**PMID:** 18377430\n**PMCID:** PMC11158672\n\n**Abstract:** The influence of three high frequency ABCB1 polymorphisms (c.1236C>T, c.2677G>A/T, and c.3435C>T) and the ABCG2 c.421C>A polymorphism on the disposition of doxorubicin in Asian breast cancer patients receiving adjuvant chemotherapy was investigated. The allelic frequency of the ABCB1 c.1236T, c.2677T, c.2677A, and c.3435T variants were 60%, 38%, 7%, and 22%, respectively, and the frequency of the ABCG2 c.421A allele was 23%. Pairwise analysis showed increased exposure levels to doxorubicin in patients harboring at least one ABCB1 c.1236T allele (P=0.03). Patients homozygous for the CC-GG-CC genotype had significantly lower doxorubicin exposure levels compared to patients who had CT-GT-CT (P=0.02) and TT-TT-TT genotypes (P=0.03). Significantly increased clearance of doxorubicin was also observed in patients harboring CC-GG-CC genotypes when compared to patients harboring the CT-GT-CT genotype (P=0.01). Patients harboring the CC-GG-CC genotypes had significantly lower peak plasma concentrations of doxorubicinol compared to patients who had TT-TT-TT genotypes (P=0.03). No significant influences on doxorubicin pharmacokinetic parameters were observed in relation to the ABCG2 c.421C>A polymorphism. The three high frequency linked polymorphisms in ABCB1 may influence doxorubicin disposition in Asian breast cancer patients.\n\n**Key content:** This pharmacokinetic study enrolled Asian (predominantly Chinese, Malay, Indian) breast cancer patients receiving FAC (fluorouracil, doxorubicin, cyclophosphamide) or FEC (fluorouracil, epirubicin, cyclophosphamide) adjuvant chemotherapy. Plasma concentrations of doxorubicin and doxorubicinol were measured. DNA genotyping was performed for ABCB1 c.1236C>T (rs1128503), c.2677G>T/A (rs2032582), c.3435C>T (rs1045642), and ABCG2 c.421C>A (rs2231142). The three ABCB1 SNPs are in strong linkage disequilibrium in Asian populations (less than in Caucasians). Haplotype analysis of the three linked ABCB1 polymorphisms showed that the CC-GG-CC haplotype (wild-type) carriers had significantly lower AUC and higher clearance of doxorubicin compared to CT-GT-CT (P=0.02) and TT-TT-TT (P=0.03) haplotype carriers. Peak plasma concentrations (Cmax) of doxorubicinol were also significantly lower in CC-GG-CC homozygotes vs TT-TT-TT (P=0.03). The ABCG2 c.421C>A polymorphism showed no significant association with doxorubicin PK. The study suggested that the ABCB1 haplotype (rather than individual SNPs) is the key determinant of doxorubicin exposure in this population.\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC11786012.md\n\n**Title:** Germline Human Leukocyte Antigen Status is Associated With Immunotherapy-Induced Pneumonitis and Treatment Response in Patients With Non-Small Cell Lung Cancer With High Programmed Death-Ligand 1 Expression\n\n**Authors:** Alvin HK Cheung, Zeta Mui, Walter W Yeung, Chit Chow, Mandy F Yu, Olivia H Chen, Kit-Yee Wong, Fuda Xie, Yat Ming Lau, Alfred S-L Cheng, Wei Kang, Ka-Fai To, Tony S Mok, Molly SC Li\n**Journal:** JTO Clinical and Research Reports\n**Date:** 2024 Oct 23\n**DOI:** 10.1016/j.jtocrr.2024.100754\n**PMID:** 39897119\n**PMCID:** PMC11786012\n\n**Abstract:** The germline human leukocyte antigen (HLA) status has been found to be associated with immunotherapy outcomes in patients with NSCLC, but its correlation to immunotherapy-induced pneumonitis and prognostic impact in the Asian population remains largely unknown. We evaluated the HLA genotype of the germline and available tumor samples in 42 patients with programmed death-ligand 1 (PD-L1) expression ≥50% undergoing pembrolizumab immunotherapy. The HLA allele expression was correlated with tumor response, disease survival, and the occurrence of pneumonitis.\n\n**Key content:** This retrospective study of 42 Asian (predominantly Hong Kong Chinese) NSCLC patients treated with first-line pembrolizumab (PD-L1 ≥50%) evaluated germline HLA genotyping. Key findings:\n\n- **Pneumonitis:** 12 patients (28.6%) developed immunotherapy-induced pneumonitis. HLA-A*02:07 allele was significantly associated with an increased risk of pneumonitis (OR=6.05, 95% CI 1.39-26.34, P=0.016). Patients with HLA-A*02:07 had a 6-fold higher risk of pneumonitis.\n- **Treatment response:** HLA-B*38:02 (P=0.029) and HLA-DQB1*03:01 (P=0.029) were significantly associated with objective response. Patients with HLA-DQA1*03:01/DQB1*03:01 haplotype were associated with better progression-free survival (PFS).\n- **Heterozygosity advantage:** Greater HLA-I heterozygosity at HLA-A, -B, and -C loci was associated with better overall survival.\n- **Tumor HLA:** Of 15 tumor samples analyzed, 6 (40%) had HLA-I copy number losses; no significant survival difference was observed for tumor HLA losses. TMB did not significantly differ among patients with different treatment outcomes.\n- The study concluded that HLA-A*02:07 is a germline biomarker for pembrolizumab-induced pneumonitis and HLA-B*38:02 and HLA-DQB1*03:01 are associated with treatment response in Asian NSCLC patients.\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC2875867.md\n\n**Title:** CYP2B6, CYP2A6 and UGT2B7 Genetic Polymorphisms are Predictors of Efavirenz Mid-dose Concentration in HIV-infected Patients\n\n**Authors:** Awewura Kwara, Margaret Lartey, Kwamena WC Sagoe, Ernest Kenu, Michael H Court\n**Journal:** AIDS (London, England)\n**Date:** 2009 Oct 23\n**DOI:** 10.1097/QAD.0b013e3283319908\n**PMID:** 19779319\n**PMCID:** PMC2875867\n\n**Abstract:** UDP-glucuronosyltransferase (UGT) 2B7 was recently identified as the main enzyme mediating efavirenz N-glucuronidation. This study determined whether selected UGT2B7 polymorphisms could enhance the prediction of efavirenz plasma concentrations from CYP2B6 and CYP2A6 genotypes. Mid-dose efavirenz plasma concentrations were determined in 94 HIV-infected Ghanaian patients at 2–8 weeks of antiretroviral therapy. UGT2B7 exon 2 SNPs c.735A>G (UGT2B7*1c; rs28365062) and c.802C>T (H268Y; UGT2B7*2; rs7439366) were determined by direct sequencing.\n\n**Key content:**\n- Study population: 94 HIV-infected Ghanaian patients on efavirenz-based antiretroviral therapy (600 mg daily).\n- CYP2B6 c.516TT genotype was the strongest predictor of high efavirenz levels, accounting for a 4,030 ng/mL increase (P<0.001).\n- UGT2B7*1a carrier status (wildtype, non-carrier of *1c or *2) was independently associated with ~475 ng/mL increase in efavirenz (P=0.004).\n- CYP2A6*9 and/or *17 carrier status was the third variable in the model, associated with 372 ng/mL increase (P=0.013).\n- The combined multivariate model predicted efavirenz log concentrations using: Log10[EFV] = 3.068 + (0.648 × CYP2B6 c.516TT) + (0.148 × UGT2B7*1a) + (0.120 × CYP2A6*9 or *17).\n- UGT2B7*2 carriers had lower efavirenz concentrations (median 1,562 ng/mL) compared to non-carriers (median 2,306 ng/mL; P=0.020).\n- In univariate analysis, CYP2B6 c.516TT genotype (P<0.001), UGT2B7*1a (P=0.046), CYP2B6*9 (P=0.019), and CYP2A6*9/*17 (P=0.030) were significantly associated.\n- The multi-gene model explained more pharmacokinetic variability than CYP2B6 genotype alone, validating UGT2B7 as a clinically relevant efavirenz-metabolizing enzyme gene.\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC3016221.md\n\n**Title:** Genetic variants in the KIF6 region and coronary event reduction from statin therapy\n\n**Authors:** Yonghong Li, Marc S Sabatine, Carmen H Tong, Ian Ford, Todd G Kirchgessner, Christopher J Packard, Michele Robertson, Charles M Rowland, Lance A Bare, James Shepherd, James J Devlin, Olga A Iakoubova\n**Journal:** Human Genetics\n**Date:** 2010 Oct 1\n**DOI:** 10.1007/s00439-010-0892-6\n**PMID:** 20886236\n**PMCID:** PMC3016221\n\n**Abstract:** Fine mapping of the KIF6 region was conducted to determine whether the previously reported rs20455 (Trp719Arg) association with differential coronary event reduction from statin therapy could be explained by another SNP and whether other independent variants predict statin response. Three tightly linked SNPs—rs20455, rs9462535, and rs9471077—were consistently associated with differential coronary event reduction from statin therapy across three prospective clinical trials.\n\n**Key content:**\n- Study population: Caucasian patients from CARE (2,913), PROVE IT-TIMI22 (1,817), and WOSCOPS (1,570) trials.\n- Statins used: pravastatin 40 mg/day (CARE, WOSCOPS) and atorvastatin 80 mg vs. pravastatin 40 mg (PROVE IT-TIMI22).\n- 170 SNPs in the KIF6 region (chr 6, 39.4–39.8 Mb) were tested.\n- Three SNPs consistently associated with differential statin response across all three studies (all P_interaction < 0.1 dominant model): rs20455 (Trp719Arg missense), rs9462535 (intronic), rs9471077 (intronic). These three SNPs are in high LD (r²=0.84–0.98).\n- Carriers of the 719Arg allele (CT+CC at rs20455; ~60% of European-ancestry population) showed significant coronary event reduction from statin therapy: CARE HR=0.67, P=0.0074; PROVE IT-TIMI22 OR=0.62, P=0.0003; WOSCOPS OR=0.50, P<0.0001. Non-carriers (TT) showed no benefit (HR/OR ≈1.0 in all studies).\n- All three SNPs were also associated with CHD risk in placebo groups.\n- The causal variant could not be definitively identified due to high LD; the missense Trp719Arg substitution (near kinesin cargo-binding domain) remains a candidate functional variant (BLOSUM62 score of -3 indicating an unlikely substitution).\n- Conclusion: KIF6 Trp719Arg (rs20455) is the best representative of a tightly linked haplotype block associated with differential coronary event reduction from statins.\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC3417133.md\n\n**Title:** The SLCO1B1*5 Genetic Variant is Associated with Statin-Induced Side Effects\n\n**Authors:** Deepak Voora, Svati H Shah, Ivan Spasojevic, Shazia Ali, Carol R Reed, Benjamin A Salisbury, Geoffrey S Ginsburg\n**Journal:** Journal of the American College of Cardiology\n**Date:** 2009 Oct 20\n**DOI:** 10.1016/j.jacc.2009.04.053\n**PMID:** 19833260\n**PMCID:** PMC3417133\n\n**Abstract:** The STRENGTH pharmacogenetics study tested reduced-function alleles of CYP2D6, CYP2C8, CYP2C9, CYP3A4, and SLCO1B1 for association with composite adverse events (CAE: discontinuation for any side effect, myalgia, or CK>3× baseline) in 509 subjects randomized to atorvastatin 10 mg, simvastatin 20 mg, or pravastatin 10 mg followed by 80 mg, 80 mg, and 40 mg, respectively.\n\n**Key content:**\n- Study population: n=509 subjects from STRENGTH study (randomized controlled trial of statin safety/efficacy).\n- Primary outcome: Composite adverse event (CAE) = discontinuation for any side effect, myalgia, or CK>3× baseline.\n- Alleles tested: CYP2D6*3, *4, *5; CYP2C8*3, *4; CYP2C9*3; CYP3A4*1b; SLCO1B1*5.\n- Only SLCO1B1*5 (rs4149056, Val174Ala) was significantly associated with the CAE:\n  - Carrier frequency: 35% in CAE group vs 25% in non-CAE (P=0.03).\n  - Allele frequency in CAE group was higher (SLCO1B1*5 MAF 28% overall).\n- Gene-dose effect confirmed: CAE proportions were 0.19 (no *5 allele, n=325), 0.27 (1 allele, n=115), and 0.50 (2 alleles, n=8); one-sided trend P=0.01.\n- SLCO1B1 rs4149080 (13th intron) showed a stronger individual association (χ²=7.5, P=0.006) but is in strong LD with *5 (r²=0.85).\n- No cytochrome P450 allele was significantly associated with the CAE.\n- The association was independent of statin type (atorvastatin, simvastatin, pravastatin) and dose, though the study was not powered for subgroup analyses.\n- This was the first prospective study to associate SLCO1B1*5 with mild statin side effects (myalgia, CK elevation without rhabdomyolysis).\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC3831180.md\n\n**Title:** SLCO1B1 Genetic Variant Associated With Statin-Induced Myopathy: A Proof-of-Concept Study Using the Clinical Practice Research Datalink\n\n**Authors:** D F Carr, H O'Meara, A L Jorgensen, J Campbell, M Hobbs, G McCann, T van Staa, M Pirmohamed\n**Journal:** Clinical Pharmacology and Therapeutics\n**Date:** 2013 Oct 2\n**DOI:** 10.1038/clpt.2013.161\n**PMID:** 23942138\n**PMCID:** PMC3831180\n\n**Abstract:** This study used the UK Clinical Practice Research Datalink (CPRD) to identify statin-induced myopathy patients (CPK > 4× ULN; n=77) and statin-tolerant controls (n=372), then tested for replication of SLCO1B1 c.521T>C (rs4149056) and COQ2 rs4693075 associations. Multiple logistic regression showed SLCO1B1 c.521T>C as a significant risk factor (P=0.009), with OR per variant allele of 2.06 (95% CI 1.32–3.15) for all myopathy and 4.09 (2.06–8.16) for severe myopathy (CPK>10×ULN and/or rhabdomyolysis; n=23). COQ2 was not associated. Meta-analysis replicated the association for simvastatin-induced myopathy.\n\n**Key content:**\n- This proof-of-concept study demonstrated that large-scale electronic medical records (CPRD, UK) can efficiently identify ADR cases for pharmacogenetics studies.\n- Case definition: statin-induced myopathy = CPK > 4× ULN during statin therapy. Cases: 77 patients (23 with severe myopathy CPK>10×ULN or rhabdomyolysis). Controls: 372 statin-tolerant patients.\n- Statin types represented: majority simvastatin users, some atorvastatin, pravastatin users.\n- SLCO1B1 rs4149056 (c.521T>C) was significantly associated (additive model): OR per C allele = 2.06 (P=0.009) for all myopathy; OR = 4.09 (P<0.001) for severe myopathy.\n- COQ2 rs4693075 was not significantly associated (P>0.05).\n- Meta-analysis of 6 predominantly Caucasian studies showed a clear association between c.521C allele and simvastatin-induced myopathy; evidence was limited for other statins.\n- Study demonstrated use of electronic health records to efficiently recruit rare ADR patients for pharmacogenetic research.\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC3876784.md\n\n**Title:** Candidate Gene Polymorphisms in Patients with Acetaminophen-Induced Acute Liver Failure\n\n**Authors:** Michael H Court, Inga Peter, Suwagmani Hazarika, Magdalini Vasiadi, David J Greenblatt, William M Lee, The Acute Liver Failure Study Group\n**Journal:** Drug Metabolism and Disposition\n**Date:** 2014 Jan\n**DOI:** 10.1124/dmd.113.053546\n**PMID:** 24104197\n**PMCID:** PMC3876784\n\n**Abstract:** This exploratory case-comparison study evaluated genotype frequency differences among patients who had developed acute liver failure (ALF) intentionally (n=78), unintentionally (n=79), or from other causes (n=103). Only CYP3A4*22 (rs35599367) was genome-wide significant. Together, CYP3A5*3 and CYP3A4*22 explained 16% of TAC trough variability; clinical variables explained 24.1%; the full model explained 40.1%. Low-frequency variants should be evaluated as potential additional contributors.\n\n**Key content:**\n- Study: DeKAF Genomics cohort; EA kidney transplant recipients; 25,255 TAC trough measurements over first 6 months.\n- GWAS platform: custom exome-plus Affymetrix TxArray SNP chip (~782,000 markers; 1,221,308 after imputation).\n- Analysis restricted to 1,345 EA recipients with 2 CYP3A5 LoF alleles (1,342 *3/*3; 2 *3/*6; 1 *3/*7), to isolate effects outside of CYP3A5.\n- Key result: Only CYP3A4*22 (rs35599367, in intron 6, reduced CYP3A4 expression) was genome-wide significant (p=2.21×10−17; beta=0.300, SE=0.035). MAF=0.054 in this EA cohort.\n- 11 additional SNPs in the CYP3A locus region (chromosome 7) were also significant but all became sub-threshold after adjustment for CYP3A4*22.\n- Variance explained:\n  - Clinical variables alone: 24.1%\n  - Clinical variables + CYP3A5*3 (rs776746): 36.6%\n  - Clinical variables + CYP3A4*22 (rs35599367): 28.5%\n  - Clinical variables + both CYP3A5*3 + CYP3A4*22: 40.1%\n  - Combined genetic contribution (CYP3A5*3 + CYP3A4*22): ~16% of total variance\n- Other previously reported candidate genes (ABCB1, POR, CYP2C19, PPARA, ABCC8, SLC28A3) were not significant in this cohort.\n- Conclusion: In EA patients with universal CYP3A5 loss-of-function, CYP3A4*22 is the only common variant with a meaningful effect on TAC troughs. The remaining ~60% of variance is unexplained, suggesting low-frequency variants detectable only by sequencing may be important.\n\n---\n\n# FILES SUMMARY\n\n**Term bank files:**\n- cancer patients\n\n**Authors:** Suman Lal, Zee Wan Wong, Edwin Sandanaraj, Xiaoqiang Xiang, Peter Cher Siang Ang, Edmund J D Lee, Balram Chowbay\n**Journal:** Cancer Science\n**Date:** 2008 Mar 28\n**DOI:** 10.1111/j.1349-7006.2008.00744.x\n**PMID:** 18377430\n**PMCID:** PMC11158672\n\n**Abstract:** The influence of three high frequency ABCB1 polymorphisms (c.1236C>T, c.2677G>A/T, and c.3435C>T) and the ABCG2 c.421C>A polymorphism on the disposition of doxorubicin in Asian breast cancer patients receiving adjuvant chemotherapy was investigated. The allelic frequency of the ABCB1 c.1236T, c.2677T, c.2677A, and c.3435T variants were 60%, 38%, 7%, and 22%, respectively, and the frequency of the ABCG2 c.421A allele was 23%. Pairwise analysis showed increased exposure levels to doxorubicin in patients harboring at least one ABCB1 c.1236T allele (P=0.03). Patients homozygous for the CC-GG-CC genotype had significantly lower doxorubicin exposure levels compared to patients who had CT-GT-CT (P=0.02) and TT-TT-TT genotypes (P=0.03). Significantly increased clearance of doxorubicin was also observed in patients harboring CC-GG-CC genotypes when compared to patients harboring the CT-GT-CT genotype (P=0.01). Patients harboring the CC-GG-CC genotypes had significantly lower peak plasma concentrations of doxorubicinol compared to patients who had TT-TT-TT genotypes (P=0.03). No significant influences on doxorubicin pharmacokinetic parameters were observed in relation to the ABCG2 c.421C>A polymorphism. The three high frequency linked polymorphisms in ABCB1 may influence doxorubicin disposition in Asian breast cancer patients.\n\n**Key content:** This pharmacokinetic study enrolled Asian (predominantly Chinese, Malay, Indian) breast cancer patients receiving FAC (fluorouracil, doxorubicin, cyclophosphamide) or FEC (fluorouracil, epirubicin, cyclophosphamide) adjuvant chemotherapy. Plasma concentrations of doxorubicin and doxorubicinol were measured. DNA genotyping was performed for ABCB1 c.1236C>T (rs1128503), c.2677G>T/A (rs2032582), c.3435C>T (rs1045642), and ABCG2 c.421C>A (rs2231142). The three ABCB1 SNPs are in strong linkage disequilibrium in Asian populations (less than in Caucasians). Haplotype analysis of the three linked ABCB1 polymorphisms showed that the CC-GG-CC haplotype (wild-type) carriers had significantly lower AUC and higher clearance of doxorubicin compared to CT-GT-CT (P=0.02) and TT-TT-TT (P=0.03) haplotype carriers. Peak plasma concentrations (Cmax) of doxorubicinol were also significantly lower in CC-GG-CC homozygotes vs TT-TT-TT (P=0.03). The ABCG2 c.421C>A polymorphism showed no significant association with doxorubicin PK. The study suggested that the ABCB1 haplotype (rather than individual SNPs) is the key determinant of doxorubicin exposure in this population.\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC11786012.md\n\n**Title:** Germline Human Leukocyte Antigen Status is Associated With Immunotherapy-Induced Pneumonitis and Treatment Response in Patients With Non-Small Cell Lung Cancer With High Programmed Death-Ligand 1 Expression\n\n**Authors:** Alvin HK Cheung, Zeta Mui, Walter W Yeung, Chit Chow, Mandy F Yu, Olivia H Chen, Kit-Yee Wong, Fuda Xie, Yat Ming Lau, Alfred S-L Cheng, Wei Kang, Ka-Fai To, Tony S Mok, Molly SC Li\n**Journal:** JTO Clinical and Research Reports\n**Date:** 2024 Oct 23\n**DOI:** 10.1016/j.jtocrr.2024.100754\n**PMID:** 39897119\n**PMCID:** PMC11786012\n\n**Abstract:** The germline human leukocyte antigen (HLA) status has been found to be associated with immunotherapy outcomes in patients with NSCLC, but its correlation to immunotherapy-induced pneumonitis and prognostic impact in the Asian population remains largely unknown. We evaluated the HLA genotype of the germline and available tumor samples in 42 patients with programmed death-ligand 1 (PD-L1) expression ≥50% undergoing pembrolizumab immunotherapy. The HLA allele expression was correlated with tumor response, disease survival, and the occurrence of pneumonitis.\n\n**Key content:** This retrospective study of 42 Asian (predominantly Hong Kong Chinese) NSCLC patients treated with first-line pembrolizumab (PD-L1 ≥50%) evaluated germline HLA genotyping. Key findings:\n\n- **Pneumonitis:** 12 patients (28.6%) developed immunotherapy-induced pneumonitis. HLA-A*02:07 allele was significantly associated with an increased risk of pneumonitis (OR=6.05, 95% CI 1.39-26.34, P=0.016). Patients with HLA-A*02:07 had a 6-fold higher risk of pneumonitis.\n- **Treatment response:** HLA-B*38:02 (P=0.029) and HLA-DQB1*03:01 (P=0.029) were significantly associated with objective response. CYP3A5 *3/*3 + SLCO1B1 C allele associated with simvastatin muscle toxicity in Uzbek patients with CAD.\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC7223759.md\n\n**Title:** Association study of genetic polymorphisms in proteins involved in oseltamivir transport, metabolism, and interactions with adverse reactions in Mexican patients with acute respiratory diseases\n\n**Authors:** Mario Bermúdez de León, Rafael B R León-Cachón, Beatriz Silva-Ramírez, Rosa Nelly González-Ríos, Brenda Escobedo-Guajardo, Roberto Leyva-Parra, Benjamín Tovar-Cisneros, Everardo González-González, Abdiel Alvarado-Díaz, Ofelia Vázquez-Monsiváis, Viviana Mata-Tijerina, Lorena Puente-Lugo, Erick Álvarez-Galván, María José Currás-Tuala, Miguel Aguado-Barrera, Fabiola Castorena-Torres, Juan Manuel Alcocer-González, Guillermo Elizondo, Ana María Salinas-Martínez\n**Journal:** The Pharmacogenomics Journal\n**Date:** 2020 Feb 4\n**DOI:** 10.1038/s41397-020-0151-8\n**PMID:** 32015454\n**PMCID:** PMC7223759\n\n**Abstract:** 310 Mexican patients with acute respiratory diseases suspected of influenza A/H1N1 were treated with oseltamivir 75 mg/day for 5 days and evaluated for adverse drug reactions (ADRs). ADRs occurred in 38 patients (12.25%): hypersensitivity (1.9%), gastritis (10%), depression/anxiety (0.9%). ABCB1-rs1045642 (C3435T) was significantly associated with ADRs under the recessive model (P=0.017); allele C was protective and allele T was associated with ADRs.\n\n**Key content:**\n- Retrospective study at IMSS clinics in Nuevo Leon, Mexico; sample collected December 2009–December 2012.\n- Drug: oseltamivir phosphate 75 mg/kg/day for ≥5 days.\n- Influenza confirmation: 130/310 (42%) positive for A/H1N1; 11 (3.5%) positive for seasonal influenza; 169 (54.5%) negative.\n- ADRs: 38 patients (12.25%): gastritis n=31 (10%), hypersensitivity n=6 (1.9%), depression/anxiety n=3 (0.9%); no seizures or hallucinations.\n- Genes/SNPs analyzed: ABCB1 (rs3789243, rs1128503, rs2032582, rs1045642), CES1 (rs71647871, rs2307243), SLC15A1 (rs2297322), NEU2 (rs2233385).\n- SNPs not in Hardy-Weinberg equilibrium (excluded from further analysis): SLC15A1-rs2297322, ABCB1-rs2032582 (G/A variant), CES1-rs2307243.\n- Association analysis results (codominant model): Only ABCB1-rs1045642 was significantly associated with ADRs (P=0.031).\n- Recessive model analysis for gastritis: ABCB1-rs1045642 C allele is protective (OR=0.395, P=0.017); T allele = increased risk of gastritis (OR=2.532, 95% CI 1.154–5.560).\n- Haplotype analysis: 4 major haplotypes identified; no significant association between haplotypes and ADRs.\n- Linkage disequilibrium: ABCB1-rs3789243 and CES1-rs71647871 in LD (P=0.029); ABCB1-rs1045642 and NEU2-rs2233385 in LD (P=0.0435).\n- Conclusion: ABCB1 rs1045642 (C3435T) is a potential predictive biomarker of ADRs in oseltamivir treatment; specifically, the T/T genotype (recessive) is associated with gastritis risk.\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC8159730.md\n\n**Title:** A systematic review and meta-analysis of genotype-based and individualized data analysis of SLCO1B1 gene and statin-induced myopathy\n\n**Authors:** Saowalak Turongkaravee, Jiraphun Jittikoon, Thitiya Lukkunaprasit, Sermsiri Sangroongruangsri, Usa Chaikledkaew, Ammarin Thakkinstian\n**Journal:** The Pharmacogenomics Journal\n**Date:** 2021 Feb 19\n**DOI:** 10.1038/s41397-021-00208-w\n**PMID:** 33608664\n**PMCID:** PMC8159730\n\n**Abstract:** Meta-analysis determining genotypic effects of SLCO1B1 rs4149056 and rs2306283 on myopathy in statin patients. Fourteen studies pooled for rs4149056; minor C allele frequency 15% in Caucasians and 14% in Asians. Six studies pooled for rs2306283; minor G allele frequency 34% in Caucasians and 75% in Asians. In Caucasians, CC genotype: OR=2.9 (95% CI 1.59–5.34); TC genotype: OR=1.6 (95% CI 1.20–2.16) vs TT. Simvastatin users: CC OR=2.8, TC OR=1.8. Atorvastatin users: CC OR=3.0, TC OR=1.6.\n\n**Key content:**\n- Systematic review methodology: PubMed, EMBASE, Cochrane, CINAHL, SCOPUS, Thai databases; studies through 2019.\n- Two independent reviewers; risk of bias assessed.\n- 14 studies included for rs4149056 meta-analysis; 6 studies for rs2306283.\n- Population: predominantly Caucasian (14 studies) and some Asian data.\n- rs4149056 allele frequency: 15% (C allele) in Caucasians, 14% in Asians.\n- rs2306283 allele frequency: 34% (G allele) in Caucasians, 75% in Asians.\n\n**rs4149056 genotypic effects in Caucasians (vs TT reference):**\n- CC genotype: pooled OR=2.9 (95% CI 1.59–5.34)\n- TC genotype: pooled OR=1.6 (95% CI 1.20–2.16)\n- TC+CC genotype: pooled OR=1.9 (95% CI 1.28–2.83)\n- Simvastatin users: CC OR=2.8 (1.17–6.77), TC OR=1.8 (1.15–2.77)\n- Atorvastatin users: CC OR=3.0 (1.02–8.93), TC OR=1.6 (1.07–2.33)\n\n**Individual patient data (IPD) mixed-effects logit model (Caucasians):**\n- CC vs TT: OR=3.8 (2.35–6.08, P<0.001)\n- TC vs TT: OR=1.8 (1.38–2.42, P<0.001)\n\n**rs2306283 effects:** No statistically significant association found in either Caucasians or Asians in genotype-based or IPD analysis.\n\n- Additional findings: Higher statin dose associated with higher myopathy risk regardless of genotype.\n- Conclusion: SLCO1B1 rs4149056 CC and TC genotypes significantly increase myopathy risk in statin users (especially simvastatin and atorvastatin); rs2306283 not significantly associated.\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC8376784.md\n\n**Title:** Effect of SLCO1B1 T521C on Statin-related Myotoxicity with Use of Lovastatin and Atorvastatin\n\n**Authors:** Brian Lu, Laura Sun, Manuel Seraydarian, Thomas J Hoffmann, Marisa W Medina, Carlos Iribarren, Ronald M Krauss, Neil Risch, Akinyemi Oni-Orisan\n**Journal:** Clinical pharmacology and therapeutics\n**Date:** 2021 Jul 23\n**DOI:** 10.1002/cpt.2337\n**PMID:** 34114646\n**PMCID:** PMC8376784\n\n**Abstract:** This study investigated whether SLCO1B1 rs4149056 genotype was associated with statin-induced myotoxicity in atorvastatin and lovastatin users using the GERA cohort. 233 cases (statin-induced myopathy+rhabdomyolysis) matched to 2,342 controls. Simvastatin CC vs TT: OR=4.6 (P=2×10−3). Lovastatin CC vs TT: OR=4.5 (P=1×10−3). Atorvastatin CC vs TT: OR=2.0 (P=0.3, not significant). All statins combined: CC vs TT OR=3.7 (P=1×10−5).\n\n**Key content:**\n- Study population: Kaiser Permanente Northern California (KPNC) GERA cohort; statin users with daily dose ≥40 mg.\n- Cases: 233 statin-induced myopathy+rhabdomyolysis cases (defined as CK>5×ULN within 6 months of statin prescription, or ICD-9 rhabdomyolysis diagnosis).\n- Controls: 2,342 matched controls (age, sex, statin type, statin dose matched). Median statin use: 1,000 days (cases), 1,040 days (controls).\n- Distribution: Simvastatin n=82 cases/748 controls; Lovastatin n=85/901; Atorvastatin n=66/693.\n- Demographics: ~72% EUR, ~12% LAT, ~9% EAS, ~7% AFR.\n\n**Primary results (myopathy+rhabdomyolysis, CC vs TT):**\n- Simvastatin: OR=4.62 (95% CI 1.58–11.9, P=0.002); TC vs TT: OR=1.78 (P=0.023). C allele frequency: 25% cases vs 15% controls (P=5×10−4).\n- Lovastatin: OR=4.49 (95% CI 1.68–10.8, P=0.001); TC vs TT: OR=1.11 (P=0.715, NS). C allele: 19% cases vs 14% controls (P=8×10−4).\n- Atorvastatin: OR=1.99 (95% CI 0.44–6.59, P=0.303, not significant); TC vs TT: OR=1.12 (P=0.716, NS). C allele: 17% cases vs 14% controls (P=0.40, NS).\n- All statins combined: TC vs TT OR=1.4 (P=0.03); CC vs TT OR=3.7 (P=1×10−5).\n\n**Secondary analysis (rhabdomyolysis alone):**\n- All statins: CC vs TT OR=3.7 (95% CI 1.97–6.75, P=2×10−5); TC vs TT OR=1.3 (NS).\n- Statin-type trends mirror primary analysis.\n\n- Sensitivity analyses matching additionally on race/ethnicity and on obesity/diabetes yielded consistent results.\n- This is the first study to examine SLCO1B1 and lovastatin-induced myotoxicity, establishing that the association extends to lovastatin. Evidence for atorvastatin was less clear (non-significant trend). CPIC guidelines currently recommend simvastatin dose adjustment for rs4149056 carriers; authors suggest considering lovastatin in updated guidelines.\n\n---\n\n## Filename: PMC8513493.md\n\n**Title:** Genome wide association study identifies the common variants in CYP3A4 and CYP3A5 responsible for variation in tacrolimus trough concentration in Caucasian kidney transplant recipients\n\n**Authors:** William S Oetting, Baolin Wu, David P Schladt, Weihua Guan, Rory P Remmel, Roslyn B Mannon, Arthur J Matas, Ajay K Israni, DeKAF Genomics Investigators\n**Journal:** The pharmacogenomics journal\n**Date:** 2017 Nov 21\n**DOI:** 10.1038/tpj.2017.49\n**PMID:** 29160300\n**PMCID:** PMC8513493\n\n**Abstract:** A GWAS was performed on TAC trough concentrations in 1,345 adult European-American (EA) kidney transplant recipients with two CYP3A5 loss-of-function alleles. Only CYP3A4*22 (rs35599367) was genome-wide significant. Together, CYP3A5*3 and CYP3A4*22 explained 16% of TAC trough variability; clinical variables explained 24.1%; the full model explained 40.1%. Low-frequency variants should be evaluated as potential additional contributors.\n\n**Key content:**\n- Study: DeKAF Genomics cohort; EA kidney transplant recipients; 25,255 TAC trough measurements over first 6 months.\n- GWAS platform: custom exome-plus Affymetrix TxArray SNP chip (~782,000 markers; 1,221,308 after imputation).\n- Analysis restricted to 1,345 EA recipients with 2 CYP3A5 LoF alleles (1,342 *3/*3; 2 *3/*6; 1 *3/*7), to isolate effects outside of CYP3A5.\n- Key result: Only CYP3A4*22 (rs35599367, in intron 6, reduced CYP3A4 expression) was genome-wide significant (p=2.21×10−17; beta=0.300, SE=0.035). MAF=0.054 in this EA cohort.\n- 11 additional SNPs in the CYP3A locus region (chromosome 7) were also significant but all became sub-threshold after adjustment for CYP3A4*22.\n- Variance explained:\n  - Clinical variables alone: 24.1%\n  - Clinical variables + CYP3A5*3 (rs776746): 36.6%\n  - Clinical variables + CYP3A4*22 (rs35599367): 28.5%\n  - Clinical variables + both CYP3A5*3 + CYP3A4*22: 40.1%\n  - Combined genetic contribution (CYP3A5*3 + CYP3A4*22): ~16% of total variance\n- Other previously reported candidate genes (ABCB1, POR, CYP2C19, PPARA, ABCC8, SLC28A3) were not significant in this cohort.\n- Conclusion: In EA patients with universal CYP3A5 loss-of-function, CYP3A4*22 is the only common variant with a meaningful effect on TAC troughs. The remaining ~60% of variance is unexplained, suggesting low-frequency variants detectable only by sequencing may be important.\n\n---\n\n# FILES SUMMARY\n\n**Term bank files:**\n-
